  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8aea3e3d-33e1-4f77-b22f-b71fb61a052f'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer2285847765366985503">A contemporary YA novel that examines rape culture through alternating perspectives. <br/><br/>Alex Craft knows how to kill someone. And she doesn’t feel bad about it.<br/><br/>Three years ago, when her older sister, Anna, was murdered and the killer walked free, Alex uncaged the language she knows best—the language of violence.   <span id="freeText2285847765366985503" style="display:none">A contemporary YA novel that examines rape culture through alternating perspectives. <br /><br />Alex Craft knows how to kill someone. And she doesn’t feel bad about it.<br /><br />Three years ago, when her older sister, Anna, was murdered and the killer walked free, Alex uncaged the language she knows best—the language of violence. While her own crime goes unpunished, Alex knows she can’t be trusted among other people. Not with Jack, the star athlete who wants to really know her but still feels guilty over the role he played the night Anna’s body was discovered. And not with Peekay, the preacher’s kid with a defiant streak who befriends Alex while they volunteer at an animal shelter. Not anyone.<br /><br />As their senior year unfolds, Alex’s darker nature breaks out, setting these three teens on a collision course that will change their lives forever.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1622748583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8309862191221290052"><blockquote>
  <i>This is how I kill someone.<br/>And I don’t feel bad about it.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>BRUTAL</b>. That's how I would describe this book. It sits there all unassuming with its cute yellow cover and pictures of animals, but underneath it has some serious fangs. Rather like the female of the species, I suppose.<br/><br/>Quick warning: this book may not be suitable to those sensitive to rape and/or animal cruelty. Make no mistake, it's a nasty book. At times it's absolutely disgustingly awful. But it's a very sharp and effective look at </span>
  <span id="freeText8309862191221290052" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>This is how I kill someone.<br />And I don’t feel bad about it.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>BRUTAL</b>. That's how I would describe this book. It sits there all unassuming with its cute yellow cover and pictures of animals, but underneath it has some serious fangs. Rather like the female of the species, I suppose.<br /><br />Quick warning: this book may not be suitable to those sensitive to rape and/or animal cruelty. Make no mistake, it's a nasty book. At times it's absolutely disgustingly awful. But it's a very sharp and effective look at sexual assault and rape culture too. And somehow <b>so fucking funny</b>. Well, maybe if you have a sadistic sense of humour, which it turns out I do.<br /><br />I don't even know how to adequately explain it. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25812109.The_Female_of_the_Species" title="The Female of the Species by Mindy McGinnis" rel="nofollow noopener">The Female of the Species</a> is told from the perspective of three different characters - Alex, whose sister was raped and murdered; Jack, the popular guy who desperately wants to get to know Alex; and Peekay, the preacher's kid whose ex-boyfriend ditched her for the beautiful Branley, and who now works at the animal shelter with Alex.<br /><br />Alex is haunted by her sister's murder. She is detached, strange, and knows there's something wrong with her. That there always has been. When she kills her sister's murderer and gets away with it, she realizes she might not be able to stop.<br /><br />It's a very <b>dark, unflinching look at rape culture, slut-shaming and the long-lasting effects of sexual assault</b>; not just on the victims, but on those close to them.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>I’m living my life waiting for the man who comes for me like one did for Anna, with hungry eyes behind the wheel and rope in the trunk.<br />I’m ready.</i>
</blockquote><br />All of the characters are so <b>complex and well-developed</b>, not just in themselves but also in their relationships with their families and each other. Obviously, we know we shouldn't agree with Alex's methods of taking the law into her own hands, but it's difficult to not adore her and see her as a kind of twisted hero. There's a lot of examples like that in this book - the fine line between what we know we should do and what we really feel.<br /><br />So many interesting tidbits about human nature are woven into the story. Alex's straight-talking unravels why we do the things we do, and the misconeptions we hold about other people and relationships. Also, <b>she does an amazing takedown of slut-shaming</b>:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"You shouldn't be that way about her," Alex says. "I hear what people say and I bet half of it isn't even true. And even if it is - fine. She's no different from you and me; she wants to have sex. So let her…She likes boys, and she can get them. You were hurt by that, but it wasn't Branley who hurt you. It was Adam."</i>
</blockquote><br />There are so many ways this could have ended, but the author chose the one that hit the hardest. Right in the feels. It's like someone just punched my heart right out of my chest. It was completely evil and the perfect ending to a book like this.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8309862191221290052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I confess I went into this book expecting a feminist, Dexter-esque, wish-fulfillment experience, and I was here for it.   <span id="freeText9989817430246618567" style="display:none">A very difficult read and some of its early chapters left me reeling. I confess I went into this book expecting a feminist, Dexter-esque, wish-fulfillment experience, and I was here for it. Instead, I got a painful, complicated, ultimately redeeming story about the insidiousness of rape culture and what it takes to dismantle it. <br /><br />Watching flawed characters grapple with learned sexism and internalized misogyny is not always a comfortable thing, and though I was surprised by some of the choices McGinnis made, I was so impressed by the way she balanced the political and the personal. <div id="review_2727308233" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2727308233" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2727308233?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2727308233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8251075529643006561">4.5 stars! This book was a TRIP!! So though-provoking and refreshing. This is a book that discusses important social issues through the lens of really well-developed characters and a suspenseful story. It taps into the darkness and brutal nature of our humanity in a way that’s jarring, but real. A book I’d highly recommend to anyone!<br/><br/>TW: sexual assault, physical assault, <br/><br/>In the week’s following me finishing the book (mind you, I finished it in two days), I felt like I read it too fast to fully pr</span>
  <span id="freeText8251075529643006561" style="display:none">4.5 stars! This book was a TRIP!! So though-provoking and refreshing. This is a book that discusses important social issues through the lens of really well-developed characters and a suspenseful story. It taps into the darkness and brutal nature of our humanity in a way that’s jarring, but real. A book I’d highly recommend to anyone!<br /><br />TW: sexual assault, physical assault, <br /><br />In the week’s following me finishing the book (mind you, I finished it in two days), I felt like I read it too fast to fully process everything that went on. I decided to read it AGAIN and basically finished in one sitting! This is absolutely a book I could read over and over and get more out of it every time. In my first reading, I actually underestimate how well constructed the story is – I felt it was lacking some development, but with a second reading, I realized how complex all components of the story are. I could not be more pleased that I finally picked this one up.<br /><br />One of my favorite things about <i>The Female of the Species</i> is that while it is a contemporary story, it reads like a thriller! Mindy McGuiness writes the story in such a chilling, atmospheric way that a sense of suspense follows you the entire time. I found it to be a very unique use of mood and tone for young adult books.<br /><br />I ADORE the characters in <i>The Female of the Species</i>. Alex is the perfect anti-hero – Vengeful resilient, and morally gray. Honestly, she can be scary at times, but she also has a soft spot where you can’t help but want the best for her. Jack was surprisingly charming. He’s the star athlete and up for valedictorian, but he’s only the perfect student because he wants to escape poverty and live a more stable life. He’s the epitome of a teenage boy, meaning he is often driven by his hormones, but he is truly a good guy with a kind heart who wants to treat others fairly. As the only protagonist, he provides a thoughtful perspective on how men react to rape culture, which was beautifully done. Peekay was also a character I wasn’t super drawn to at the start, but she quickly grew on me. I loved watching her character growth as she gained awareness of herself and the people around her. It also plays with some high school stereotypes as a way to break them down which I appreciated seeing. The characters in this book are so multifaceted while still retaining the authentic nature of teenagers, which left me really impressed.<br /><br /><i>The Female of the Species</i> is incredibly thematic. It examines the lines between right and wrong, human nature and animal instinct, justice and corruption. It provides a thoughtful commentary on rape culture, the treatment of women, slut-shaming, and feminism. If gender equality and just treatment for sexual abusers are things you care about, this is an absolute MUST read.<br /><br />This book was REALLY REALLY great. I’m super excited to read more from Mindy McGuiness based on my first experience with her work. The refreshing writing, well-rounded characters, social commentary, and intoxicating plot work together perfectly to create a book that will remain at the top of my recommendations list for young adult contemporaries.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8251075529643006561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1729543249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1729543249" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1729543249?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062320896" href="/book/show/28512548-the-female-of-the-species">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=harpercollins">harpercollins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=thriller-suspense">thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=questionable-ethics">questionable-ethics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2016-publication">2016-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2016-favorites">2016-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=mature-ya">mature-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=heroines-butt-kicking">heroines-butt-kicking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=september">september</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1729543249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5354707469951357697"><i>"You see it in all animals - the female of the species is more deadly than the male."</i><br/><br/><b>4.5 stars</b> Holy shit, this is good. It sounds like it's going to be a <b>revenge thriller</b>, and it is--but it's also a <b>searing takedown of rape culture</b> and a merciless examination of the way violence begets violence. Riveting prose, three clear POVs, and a relentless story that doesn't try to provide answers, but forces you to think about the things we excuse legally and socially. In a year in which we've stood by an</span>
  <span id="freeText5354707469951357697" style="display:none"><i>"You see it in all animals - the female of the species is more deadly than the male."</i><br /><br /><b>4.5 stars</b> Holy shit, this is good. It sounds like it's going to be a <b>revenge thriller</b>, and it is--but it's also a <b>searing takedown of rape culture</b> and a merciless examination of the way violence begets violence. Riveting prose, three clear POVs, and a relentless story that doesn't try to provide answers, but forces you to think about the things we excuse legally and socially. In a year in which we've stood by and watched Brock Turner get a slap on the wrist, seen serial abusers publicly disparage the victims they attacked, and witnessed the repeated objectification of women on a national platform, this could not be more timely. I wish this book were in the hands of all teenagers, boys and girls, for the invaluable conversation piece that it is. There are a fair number of contemporary YA "issue" novels that deal with rape or abuse, but this one, in the guise of a thriller, hits home intellectually and emotionally in a way I haven't seen before. <br /><br /><i>But </i>boys will be boys<i>, our favorite phrase that excuses so many things, while the only thing we have for the opposite gender is </i>women<i>, said with disdain and punctuated with an eye roll.</i><br /><br />There are a few things you have to accept for the purposes of the story, the biggest of which is a logistical issue <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[namely, that physically, it's not that easy to do the things Alex did to Comstock <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I'm okay with looking past that, however, because the author provides enough convincing detail to make it worthwhile. The only thing that really niggles me a bit (aside from a slightly rushed ending) is that, in my view, Alex's feelings for Jack develop and progress a bit too quickly to fit the <b>near-feral, loner mindset</b> she was in. There's definitely chemistry between them, but I was still never fully convinced the two of them would have been a thing that quickly, especially considering his background and baggage. However, I liked that Alex didn't judge Jack or other girls for his past, I liked the way a real obstacle came between them <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that is, that he had a real problem absorbing the disturbing information she revealed to him; too many books let the BF/GF give the MC a pass <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and I liked the fantastic way the story ended. OVARIES OF STEEL, Ms. McGinniss. <br /><br />Bonus: there isn't the faintest whiff of the type of pretentious posturing and tiresome smoke-and-mirrors plotting that's become so popular in YA thrillers lately. (I'm looking at you, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16143347.We_Were_Liars" title="We Were Liars by E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">We Were Liars</a>.) This book has things to say, and the writing cuts like a razor so that <b>words nearly bleed off the page</b>.<br /><br />I'm really pissed off at the weirdly quirky cover art for this book, however. WTF is that? It does absolutely no justice to the intensity of the blistering words and emotions inside. This book is <b>full of feminine rage</b>, and while some readers might flinch at the violence within, I think it's rage that's been justly earned. <br /><br /><b>Trigger warnings</b> for violence, sexual and otherwise.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5354707469951357697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2107371972" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2107371972" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2107371972?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062320896" href="/book/show/28512548-the-female-of-the-species">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2107371972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12242521907424911491"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1557852788i/27506971._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Be prepared<br/><br/><img alt=' ' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504014551i/23717661._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I just wasn't going to read this book. I just wasn't. I bought it because I thought it was going to be something I liked. Then I saw some warnings about things in the book and I thought, if I pick up this book I'm going to throw it across the room. I almost did a few times. <br/><br/>BUT<br/><br/>I didn't<br/><br/>and I loved it<br/><br/>All of the animal abusers and rapists of any sort should burn. It's just that simple. <br/><br/><img alt=' ' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467398680ra/19588748.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img alt=' ' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504014551ra/23717662.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>and I really don't care if no one feels the same as I do. I just don't care any more. <br/><br/>I loved Alex Craf</span>
  <span id="freeText12242521907424911491" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1557852788i/27506971._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Be prepared<br><br><img alt=" " src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504014551i/23717661._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just wasn't going to read this book. I just wasn't. I bought it because I thought it was going to be something I liked. Then I saw some warnings about things in the book and I thought, if I pick up this book I'm going to throw it across the room. I almost did a few times. <br><br>BUT<br><br>I didn't<br><br>and I loved it<br><br>All of the animal abusers and rapists of any sort should burn. It's just that simple. <br><br><img alt=" " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467398680ra/19588748.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img alt=" " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504014551ra/23717662.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and I really don't care if no one feels the same as I do. I just don't care any more. <br><br>I loved Alex Craft. I wish she was my best friend. She's my role model. She's a murderer. She hurts evil people and she cares for animals. I love her. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>This is how I kill someone.<br>I learn his habits, I know his schedule. It is not difficult. His life consists of quick stops to the dollar store for the bare minimum of things required to keep this ragged cycle going, his hat pulled down over his eyes so as not to be recognized.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Alex had a sister once. She was raped, tortured and killed. Yes, it is graphic, the telling of what was done to her and how they found her in pieces. The b@stard was not sentenced. But he was killed. They let that slide. <br><br>This story is about Alex, Peekay (Preacher's Kid, real name, Claire) and Jack. There are some other people in the book, their friends, but it's mainly about them. <br><br>Alex and Peekay work at the animal shelter together and they become friends. Alex calls her by her real name. Alex is different and I like her. Alex takes care of the animals with a tender heart. Once again, I love her. They had to go and pick up some puppies that were thrown out of a window by some piece of sh*t. Peekay has thoughts of bodily harm herself but they are only thoughts. I can understand what she means. <br><br><b>I imagine a rusted-out truck, a guy wearing a T-shirt with ripped-out sleeves. I think about how he'd roll down his window, a casual question on his face until I opened the door, drag him out, and kick him in the gut over and over until he's making the same noises those puppies probably made.</b><br><br>Jack is just a guy at school that sleeps around but starts to fall for Alex. Alex has never had a boyfriend. She's too damaged and dangerous, but that doesn't mean she can't love. And they do, for a time. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>The books didn't help me find a word for myself; my father refused to accept the weight of it. And so I made my own. <br><br>I am vengeance.</blockquote>
</b><blockquote>
<br><br>This story has so many things going for it. I love the author's writing. You feel every little thing these kids go through. Even the few times the parents are in the book. All of these kids learn to be friends in one sense or another. I love that they can put all of the things aside and just be friends. <br><br>I love that Alex is so tough and never backs down from taking up for her friends. For someone that never really had any, she's a damn great one to have. Peekay thought so too. <br><br><b><blockquote>No, I didn't know. Everyone else wants to talk about the Alex who tore Ray Parson's nose off when he tried to hurt me, the Alex who tortured the man who killed her sister, the Alex who burned a child molester alive and blew a rapist away with a shotgun blast. Nobody wants to talk about the girl who held kittens in the palm of her hand, humming to them while they fed, or the girl who would pick fleas off a dog for hours. Because nobody knew her.</blockquote></b>
</blockquote><br><br>This book truly got to me. I loved everyone and hated many. It made me rage and cry. It tore my feels into a million pieces. It is one of my favorites. <br><br>READ THIS BOOK! <br><br><img alt=" " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504014551ra/23717663.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending broke my heart =( <br><br>Mel 🖤🐶🐺🐾<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/08/the-female-of-species-by-mindy-mcginnis.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1720503519" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1720503519" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1720503519?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062320896" href="/book/show/28512548-the-female-of-the-species">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=pretty-girls-make-graves">pretty-girls-make-graves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=girls-gone-wild">girls-gone-wild</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=from-publisher-or-author">from-publisher-or-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1720503519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer303019117570522108"><b>congratulations! semifinalist in goodreads' best young adult fiction category 2016!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470487819i/19934214.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>meets <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471042732i/19995075._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>where to fucking begin?<br/><br/>this is going to be a hugely polarizing book. if you're easily made squeamish by naughty language, depictions of teenagers drinking, doing drugs, having sex, or by violence (animal, people, sexual) or are otherwise a highly sensitive person, this book will probably play too rough for you. but considering how very often some of the events covered in this book make the news, the <i>world</i> p</span>
  <span id="freeText303019117570522108" style="display:none"><b>congratulations! semifinalist in goodreads' best young adult fiction category 2016!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470487819i/19934214.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>meets <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471042732i/19995075._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>where to fucking begin?<br><br>this is going to be a hugely polarizing book. if you're easily made squeamish by naughty language, depictions of teenagers drinking, doing drugs, having sex, or by violence (animal, people, sexual) or are otherwise a highly sensitive person, this book will probably play too rough for you. but considering how very often some of the events covered in this book make the news, the <i>world</i> probably plays too rough for you. <br><br>this book is important, honest, and in many ways realistic and it should be required reading for teenagers, but especially for teen girls. it's definitely full of lessons boys should learn, but there are even more here for girls. i say "lessons" like it's some kind of staid primer on etiquette, but it is far from that. it's a gritty whipcrack of a book that has strong characters and story, but is also peppered with frank depictions about all the insidious ways rape culture manifests in the day-to-day, and about gender, behavior, teen sexualization, peer pressure, slut-shaming, jealousy, sexting, and female rage.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471042732ra/19995076.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>i will likely reference this movie a lot in the course of this review. <br><br>this story is told from three first-person POVs: alex craft, who found her own path to justice when her older sister's rapist/murderer walked on a technicality - and then never walked again, peekay, the preacher's kid; the epitome of girl next door, but the <i>actual</i> girl next door, not the stereotypical angel - she'll drink and is pro push-up bra, and she's representing everygirl here, and jack - the golden boy who has looks, smarts, popularity, talent, the cheerleader on his arm, a colorful sexual history and now, an interest in alex. <br><br><i>I want to know what she looks like with tousled hair. I want to know what the scar on her wrist is from. I understand now why my mom always asks me if I'm <b>interested</b> in any girls as opposed to if I <b>like</b> them.<br><br>I like Branley. I've always liked Branley.<br><br>I'm interested in Alex.</i><br><br>after her sister anna was killed, and alex gave in to her darker impulses, she's remained on the sidelines of the high school experience; the perfect vantage point to study the oftentimes disturbing interactions of her peers. when she and peekay unexpectedly become friends, she illuminates some of her findings to peekay, pointing out the ways peekay has been unconsciously contributing to the "boys will be boys" attitude that ends up hurting girls and poisoning the sisterhood. she doesn't use that word, but she's definitely a feminist mouthpiece whose lectures would perhaps be off-putting if they weren't coming from a mostly likable character whose odd way of talking is largely due to experiencing life through books instead of getting her teen socialization in a more traditional way. <br><br>throughout the book, there are many examples of disturbing behavior that has become normalized - nude photos sent to an ex by a girl dating someone else, to reel him in for some nostalgic casual sex, locker-room details about what female classmates look like naked and what noises they make during intercourse, girls bathroom-graffiti tearing down other girls, girls determining their own worth in terms of sexual currency, being oddly pleased when guys look at your tits when talking to you, or ogle them without the courtesy of a conversation, bitchy remarks over the provocative way another girl is dressed. (<i>"She looks nice,"</i> says alex), slut-shaming the girl who "stole" peekay's boyfriend, <br><br><i>"You shouldn't be that way about her," Alex says. "I hear what people say and I bet half of it isn't even true. And even if it is - fine. She's no different from you and me; she wants to have sex. So let her…She likes boys, and she can get them. You were hurt by that, but it wasn't Branley who hurt you. It was Adam."</i><br> <br>and it's accepting all these thoughtless behaviors that perpetuates the dynamic where girls turn on other girls instead of holding boys accountable for their actions.<br><br><i>Tonight they used words they know, words that don't bother people anymore. They said bitch. They told another girl they would put their dicks in her mouth. No one protested because this is our language now.</i><br><br>some of the examples were a bit on the prudish side. yes, the guy humping the basketball was maybe sexualizing gym class in a way that someone would find uncomfortable, but we don't know what gender he was imagining that basketball to be, and sex-gestures are not made by boys alone. i've been known to make handy or blowie gestures or even full on penetrating motions, even though i do not have a penis of my own. sex miming is not always threatening or violent, it depends on the context. it's juvenile, sure, but i mean no harm when i make jerkoff motions in place of saying "whatever." <br><br>but, whatever. or, rather:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471103515ra/20002287.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>over the course of the book, as alex establishes her first friendship with peekay and her first relationship with jack, these positive emotions bring her other, darker, emotions closer to the surface. she is fiercely protective of peekay, and when she is threatened one night, <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471042732ra/19995079.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>alex uncages the beast. but it's not always easy to put that beast back in its cage. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471042732i/19995082._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>it's definitely a firecracker of a book. but whatever you do, do not call alex a firecracker!<br><br><i>…he said, "How's my little firecracker?"<br><br>Like it was a joke, this thing inside me. A cute quirk for a girl to have, our dark leanings reduced to one word.<br><br>So I said, "I'm fine."<br><br>I'm not fine, and I doubt I ever will be.<br><br>The books didn't help me find a word for myself; my father refused to accept the weight of it. And so I made my own.<br><br>I am vengeance.</i> <br><br>and she's just excellent at being vengeance.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471042732i/19995080._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>it's not all horror and violence - there are bright shiny spots of hope and positivity. there is a scene with peekay and her friend sara having a tricky conversation with peekay's parents that is both hilarious and emotional and an example of excellent parenting.<br><br>and the relationships between all of the female characters, as trust grows and resentments change, is beautifully, naturalistically, handled. alex and jack's romance is also sweet, in the way it changes jack's priorities and allows alex some happiness, albeit a complicated happiness.<br><br><i>I text Alex and tell her good night, she responds with the same, and I hold my phone tightly, too aware that the present is all we have if I can't mention the past and she won't talk about the future.</i><br><br>but alex is a complicated kind of girl - she's lived through an experience that shattered her family - turning her mother into an alcoholic who never leaves the house,<br><br><i>Nothing is ours; nothing is sacred. The one thing we shared was pulled into pieces, memorialized and mythologized so that everyone could participate in it. When she was missing, Anna's picture was tacked in so many places around town it's what I see when I think of her, not her actual face. I see that picture next to a lost cat poster and a lawn-mowing service advertisement.<br><br>I learned later they did find that cat.</i><br><br>and has darkened her entire worldview<br><br><blockquote>Anna told me I would understand about boys one day. She said that everything would change and I would look at them differently, assess their bodies and their words, the way their eyes moved when they talked to me. She said I'd not only want to answer them, but I'd learn how, knowing which words to use, how to give meaning with a pause.<br><br>Then a man took her.<br><br>A man took her before I learned any of these things. He took her and kept her for a while, put things inside of her. Of course the obvious thing, but also some others, like he was curious if they'd fit. Then he got bored. Then he got creative.<br><br>Then my sister was gone and I thought: <i>I understand about boys now.</i><br><br>And she was right. Everything did change. I look at them differently and I assess their bodies and watch their eyes and weigh their words.<br><br>But not in the way she meant.</blockquote><br><br>this book definitely left its mark on me. i murmured "holy shit" several times while reading it, because it is SO FAR beyond what YA lit of my youth was,and the fact that books like this are necessary (and they are), is depressing.<br><br>it's not perfect - i have some logic-questions, and alex is just a little <i>too</i> knowing for her age and experiences, but a book that reminds girls to be cautious and self-respecting and to call dudes out on their bullshit, and reminds guys to be respect<i>ful</i> and that stupid decisions have consequences, well - i'm a fan.<br><br>not everyone will appreciate being punched in the face by a book. <br><br>but i do.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="303019117570522108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=unreliable-characters">unreliable-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=rape-culture">rape-culture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=teen-drama">teen-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2371539824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13220334507622189445">The book world needs unreliable characters.<br/><br/>Because it’s not true that you can trust anyone you meet. These characters teach you to stay vigilant and make sure you know the person you’re with inside out before you give them access to your precious heart. <br/><br/>Plus they’re <i>very</i> entertaining. <br/><br/>Alex Craft is not your typical teenage girl. She may seem like she is at first glance, but then you hear her talk and you notice her eerie stillness and suddenly you’re not sure anymore who’s the person in front of</span>
  <span id="freeText13220334507622189445" style="display:none">The book world needs unreliable characters.<br /><br />Because it’s not true that you can trust anyone you meet. These characters teach you to stay vigilant and make sure you know the person you’re with inside out before you give them access to your precious heart. <br /><br />Plus they’re <i>very</i> entertaining. <br /><br />Alex Craft is not your typical teenage girl. She may seem like she is at first glance, but then you hear her talk and you notice her eerie stillness and suddenly you’re not sure anymore who’s the person in front of you.<br /><br />She’s a killer. She murdered the murderer who murdered and raped her sister. Well that was a mouthful, but just in case you haven’t gotten the message yet: Alex Craft has some demons inside of her that are itching to get out… again. <br /><br />One would say that she is ridding the world of its nasty creatures (aka the rapists), but that doesn’t change the fact that she ended someone’s life and now she’s trying to be a normal teenager again? It doesn’t work that way. Maybe for a psychopath or a sociopath, but is that really who Alex is?<br /><br />This is familiar, and yet so unlike any YA contemporary book I have read before. It is familiar because there is high school drama and boy drama and thirsty, disgusting boys who can’t keep it in their pants and simply must jump on everything that moves.<br /><br />But then there’s Alex Craft who fights, quite violently, to stop the normalization of rape (‘‘boys will be boys’’) that becomes more and more prevalent every time someone fails to denounce it. Her friends Peekay and Jack also find ways of exposing rape culture for what it is: an abomination, though in more innocuous ways than Alex does. They learn from each other slowly but surely and help each other grow into informed adults. <br /><br />I’m looking around at other responses to this story, and almost everyone mentions how ‘‘dark’’ and ‘‘gut-wrenching’’ this book is. While I agree that it is not an easy read and, of course, unpredictable from start to finish (impossible for it not to be when you have a character like Alex Craft), it’s also somewhat quiet… and slow. There is little action, the characters’ ever-evolving thoughts being the focus of the story. By ‘‘quiet,’’ I mean that most of it is like the calm before the storm… though the storm certainly does eventually come. <br /><br />I was supposed to read this one when I was granted access to an early copy, but as you can see I decided to wait two years instead. Because why not. Because sometimes you don’t really think it’s going to be that good and you want to postpone the disappointment as much as possible, even when what actually awaits you is a powerful new outlook on a topic that should stop being taboo. Rape needs to be discussed <b>so it can be broken apart</b>. Don’t fear the word. Understand it and fight against it, too. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13220334507622189445" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1416183174" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1416183174" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1416183174?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2016">best-of-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1416183174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8709068760422157685"><b>DO YOU SEE THAT PUDDLE OF PUNCTURED FEELS IN THE CORNER?? THAT'S ME.</b> It's okay. I didn't want HAPPINESS ANYWAY. Omg. To all of you who said: <i>Hey Cait! That's an excellent book! I hope you like it!</i> WELL LET ME SMACK YOU IN THE FACE. HOW DARE YOU NOT WARN ME. OMG.<br/><br/>Also, if you are reading this review and haven't read the book: Hey! This is an excellent book! I hope you like it!<br/><br/>(AKA I hope you suffer like I am suffering right now omgggggg.)<br/><br/><b>Basically the is one of the best contemporaries I've read in</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8709068760422157685" style="display:none"><b>DO YOU SEE THAT PUDDLE OF PUNCTURED FEELS IN THE CORNER?? THAT'S ME.</b> It's okay. I didn't want HAPPINESS ANYWAY. Omg. To all of you who said: <i>Hey Cait! That's an excellent book! I hope you like it!</i> WELL LET ME SMACK YOU IN THE FACE. HOW DARE YOU NOT WARN ME. OMG.<br /><br />Also, if you are reading this review and haven't read the book: Hey! This is an excellent book! I hope you like it!<br /><br />(AKA I hope you suffer like I am suffering right now omgggggg.)<br /><br /><b>Basically the is one of the best contemporaries I've read in a long time.</b> Mostly because it effortlessly balances (A) excellent moral questions, (B) commentates on how rape-culture and how disgusting our society is with it's apatheticness to it, (C) is completely morally-grey, (D) STABBINESS, and (E) has some of the most complex and amazing characters I've ever read. Like wow wow wow. This book blew me away. And I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13112869.Not_a_Drop_to_Drink__Not_a_Drop_to_Drink___1_" title="Not a Drop to Drink (Not a Drop to Drink, #1) by Mindy McGinnis" rel="nofollow noopener">Not a Drop to Drink</a>, but I still didn't expect this much awesome here?! SILLY ME.<br /><br />(Although what is up with the cover, dude? It is not cool.)<br /><br /><b>We have to talk about the characters, though, because they're the best part.</b> It's actually narrated by 3 people. Which usually I don't like???? But here I absolutely freaking loved it??? (Seriously if you loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22752127.The_Serpent_King" title="The Serpent King by Jeff Zentner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Serpent King</a> THEN YOU MUST READ THIS IMMEDIATELY.) And as amazing, complex, and interesting as the main characters were -- even <b>the secondary characters were incredible.</b> THAT takes talent. But let's just run through the main ones shall we?<br />• <b>ALEX:</b> Her sister was raped and murdered a few years before the story begins, and she's basically been hermiting ever since. She's a very INTENSE person. Like that's how people always describe her. She looks at you to long, she isn't emotional, she's very factual, and she talks like a book because she reads more than peoples. And she totally 100% murdered her sister's killer. Like <b>Alex is one of my new favourite characters.</b> Because omg. She loved and cared for puppies, she never EVER let anyone get away with a rape joke. She will smack down boys just for slurring another girl. She was the Vigilante Batman of Feminism. AND LIKE VERY MORALLY GREY. Is it ever okay to take justice into your own hands? I just...afjdskald....the way she was written was PERFECT and CAPTIVATING and CHILLING.<br />•<b> PEEKAY:</b> She's the preacher's kid (ergo "PK") and she's suffering from a bad breakup. She's also trying to distance herself from her father's church. By drinking. Mostly. Like, I didn't really understand what Peekay had against her family/religion? It wasn't really explained. Her parents were really darn awesome and loved her and yet....YEAh. I just wish it had explained WHY she was so intensely opposed to being a PK but yet <i>the only name she answered to was Peekay</i>. Okay. BUT DESPITE ALL OF THAT SHE WAS SO AMAZING. I LOVED HER. She was complex and interesting and just afjdksald. She loved animals and she drew Alex out of her shell and she was strong and her character development was A+.<br /><b>• JACK:</b> Okay, I'm a bit doomed to love characters named Jack...because I LOVE THE NAME JACK. (Shh this is logical.) But like, he was a bit of a completely idiot. As <i>he</i> so nicely put it: he basically drank too much and thought with his dick instead of his brain. Hmm. But he was still so complexly written! AND CHARACTER DEVELOPMENT. Also A++. I didn't like everything he did, or what he thought, or his decision making. But he was still an amazingly written character and I think I'm crying a little over his and Alex's relationship and slow-burn romance. &lt;3 Bless this.<br /><br /><b>Also with the secondary characters...I really like how Branley was written.</b> She's the "plastic beautiful girl", you know? The mean girl. WHICH IS SO EASY TO DO IN A VERY CLICHE WAY BUT NOPE. NOT HERE. Branley uses sex to get what she wants, but she's actually terrified of being stupid and tossed away. She loves her little sister. She has a dog. She's like a <i>person</i>, not just this plastic prom queen, and even though SHE'S ABSOLUTELY HORRIBLE AT TIMES, the book said "hey everyone is human. Look. Human. Feelings. Let's see all the sides of the story" and I appreciate that.<br /><br /><b>Speaking of romance: IT'S BEAUTIFUL.</b> Although it'll also punch you in the gut, so. <b>But I don't really think the book is focused on romance.</b> It does talk a lot, and very openly about sex. Particularly sex culture (is that a thing?? Eesh I don't even know) but it just smacks down the "boys will be boys" mantra. And it discusses alcohol addictions and rape culture. And <b>it's so freaking feministic that my heart is just singing.</b><br /><br /><b>SMALL LIST OF OTHER THINGS I LOVED:</b><br />• It's set quite a lot in a vet and animal shelter! SO THERE ARE MANY DOGS AND PUPPIES AND KITTENS AND AJFDKSLAFD.<br />• It actually has a huge cast of characters but I loved it so much.<br />• It's written so effortlessly beautifully, with poignant sentences and lyrical prose at times that just knocked me flat.<br />• The story is 100% captivating. Usually I get bored in contemporaries BUT NOT THIS TIME.<br />• There is blood.<br />• And murder.<br />• And situations that will make your brain just start screaming.<br />• IT IS REALLY DARK AND REALLY GRITTY.<br /><br /><br /><b>SMALL LIST OF THINGS I DIDN'T LIKE:</b><br />• Okay, well...in the finale there was a bit of a surprisingly "coincidental" situation that confused me and I'm still squinting at it.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Like the two rapists from the party....how did they even manage to show up at the church JUST at that moment??? Like, really? Why were they there? What were the chances? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />• There is so much drinking. Like OMG WHY DON'T YOU PEOPLE SEE WHAT IT'S DOING. They can have endless adults saying "hey drinking + parties in the dark woods = very good chance someone is going to be raped" and the teens all like naaaaaaaaah. *SMACKS THEM UPSIDE THE HEAD* Which I guess is a very realistic teen attitude. So. I just don't understand why people drink so much and destroy themselves, but whatever.<br />• The ending has not got a lot of closure. Boo.<br /><br /><b>ALSO DID I MENTION MY FEELS ARE SMASHED INTO A MILLION PIECES???</b> I HURT I HURT I HURT. This is a very emphatic positive, by the way. And I feel like this book is going to stay with me for a long time. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I actually legit thought that Jack was going to die?? I was actually all geared up for that, BUT I GUESS IT MAKES SENSE THAT IT WAS ALEX WHO DIED. Even though my heart is broken omg. I mean, she killed people. It probably would've had to catch up with her eventually. But I still <i>am crying</i> that she died. She was BATMAN and she was intense, and serious, and took no shit and just....Alex. omg. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL: I'm only going to say <i>READ THIS BOOK</i> because that's all that needs to be said.</b> Hahah, I mean, I just wrote a massive rambly review. But whatever. That's what you need to take away: READ THIS BOOK. It's poignant, it's beautifully written, the characters are <i>amazing</i>, the writing is INCREDIBLE. It commentates on society's warped standards and it's realistic and <b>brutal and bloody.</b> And there's puppies. There is literally no downside.<br /><br />** QUOTES **<br /><br /><blockquote>But <i>boys will be boys</i>, our favourite phrase that excuses so many things, while the only thing we have for the opposite gender is <i>women</i> said with disdain and punctuated with an eye roll.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Define success," I say almost to myself.<br />"I didn't kill anyone today," Alex says.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>I've tried to find out, looked up the words and the phrases that seemed as if they should fit. Words like <i>sociopath</i> and <i>psychopath</i>, ones that people like to toss around without knowing what they actually mean. But neither of them fits. They spoke of lack of empathy, disregarding the safety of others -- when I am the opposite.<br />I feel too much.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>Alex doesn't hesitate. The answer is right on her lips, like she's had it prepped in anticipation. <br />"I read a lot. I don't have a lot of experience in conversation, so my turn of phrase is different from..."<br />"Pretty much everybody else, yeah," I finish.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>My violence is everywhere here.<br />And I like it. </blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="8709068760422157685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2177414397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2177414397" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2177414397?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=1-and-a-half-stars">1-and-a-half-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=comments">comments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=couldn-t-wait-to-read">couldn-t-wait-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=nope">nope</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2177414397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1159821234657538021">Okay. Before we get into this, I just want to say that the lens through which I’ll be judging this book feels unfair even to me (and that’s saying something because I rain hell on young adult contemporaries like they’re calling themselves the 21st century <i>Ulysses</i>), but the book brought it on itself! <br/><br/>(<b>Note</b>: At the moment, there are unmarked spoilers in the comments of this review. Please be aware so you don't spoil yourself.)<br/><br/>I went through the entirety of this thing thinking it was just ya averag</span>
  <span id="freeText1159821234657538021" style="display:none">Okay. Before we get into this, I just want to say that the lens through which I’ll be judging this book feels unfair even to me (and that’s saying something because I rain hell on young adult contemporaries like they’re calling themselves the 21st century <i>Ulysses</i>), but the book brought it on itself! <br /><br />(<b>Note</b>: At the moment, there are unmarked spoilers in the comments of this review. Please be aware so you don't spoil yourself.)<br /><br />I went through the entirety of this thing thinking it was just ya average contemporary. I finished it being like, <i>Um, okay, that was, uh...kinda weird</i>, but I wasn’t ANGRY or anything. (Pretty rare for a just-finished-a-contemporary version of me!)<br /><br />Then I read the synopsis. Particularly this little first-line number:<br /><br /><i>A contemporary YA novel that examines rape culture through alternating perspectives. </i><br /><br />Uh.<br /><br />The f*ck?<br /><br />If this is supposed to be an examination of rape culture, LITERALLY WHAT. It could not be more sloppy. If you told me, “This was an edgy, kind of gritty contemporary, and then the publisher told the author to make rape culture a theme 45 minutes before it was due to the bookbinder, or whatever we do to physically print books in 2017,” I’d be like, yeah, okay. <br /><br />In other words, this is exclusively an impressive look at rape culture in that incredibly specific hypothetical I just made up in which the time frame is roughly as long as the amount of time it takes to make brownies.<br /><br />NEVER IN MY LIFE HAVE I SEEN SUCH A SLOPPY TAKE ON AN IMPORTANT ISSUE. NEVER IN MY LIFE HAVE I SEEN A MORE TERRIBLY WRAPPED UP ATTEMPT AT DEPTH AND PROFOUNDNESS.<br /><br />(The caps lock is to symbolize the fact that I actually literally screamed out those words as I typed them. In real, actual life.)<br /><br />There are a bunch of reasons why this is an unsatisfactory, incomplete, <s>terrible</s> examination of rape culture. Let’s talk about some of them.<br /><br /><b>ONE</b>: Bringing in negative elements of rape culture without fully condemning or resolving them<br /><br />There’s a sh*t ton of girl hate in this book. There is a hell of a lot of slut-shaming. The most consistent villain (in spite of the presence of murderers, rapists, and absentee parents) is a cheerleader. <br /><br />All of this could be useful if it were condemned. Or if character development hit those who were participating in it. Or even if somebody went to Hallmark, bought an I’m Sorry card and f*cking signed it.<br /><br />BUT NONE OF THAT HAPPENS. Because the ending occurs like 6 pages after the climax. SO NOTHING IS RESOLVED. More on that later.<br /><br /><br /><b>TWO</b>: Rape culture is just this thing that exists, intrinsically part of society, for reasons no one is aware of<br /><br />Who the ever-living hell cares about an “““examination of rape culture””” if it offers no goddamn explanation for its existence? This book just, like, kind of sort of shows what rape culture is (if rape culture were to exist in a world populated with the most unrealistic, improbable humans of all time - but we’ll talk more about that later) without offering any reasoning as to why it’s a part of our society. NO FORM OF BIGOTRY IS AN ISLAND AS THEY SAY.<br /><br />I’m halfway into a beginner level gender class and I can offer bare minimum four gender study terms off the top of my head! Which is, guess what, four more than this book even hints at! (This is not a brag; I am not an intellectual of gender studies. I literally do not even do the readings in that class.)<br /><br /><br /><b>THREE</b>: Rape culture is just here forever, intrinsically part of society, and there are no solutions ever at all sorry!!<br /><br />Speaking of things that are an intrinsic part of societal examinations that are full-on not included in this book: We are offered <i>no solutions</i>. THE MAIN CHARACTER OF THIS BOOK MURDERS PEOPLE. That’s the closest we get to a “hey guys, here’s how we can stop this.” Actual, full-on, first-degree murder!!!!!!<br /><br />We don’t even get a moral! I fought tooth and nail through 352 pages and we don’t even get a sense of what we can do, or how we can end this, or even how we can treat each other better. (Because, again: Unresolved girl hate. Yippee.)<br /><br /><br /><b>FOUR</b>: That f*cking ending!!!!<br /><br />Almost all of my problems with this book stem from its sh*tty excuse for a conclusion. It’s like allllllll of the sudden, this book drops the self-importance and decides, “Hey wait, can we go back to that gritty contemporary idea??? That sounds better??? Less hard to definitively end????”<br /><br />This ending features <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a brutal, gruesome death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, nobody healing from the events, no idea of the future, no concrete solutions, no moral on rape culture, no ANYTHING ON RAPE CULTURE. Alex becomes famous for being a f*cking vigilante or whatever, which is so stupid I nearly went blind from dumbness overload, and then it just. Ends.<br /><br />And I hate it. SO much.<br /><br /><br /><b>FIVE</b>: What the hell with these characters, man<br /><br />An evil, obsessive cheerleader. A numb girl-murderer. Some jock with a heart of gold, maybe, but really just a d*ck that REFUSES to quit. <i>A girl whose literal nickname is PK, for Preacher’s Kid</i>, because that would definitely not only be widespread enough to warrant everyone recognizing it but FOR THE GIRL HERSELF TO ADOPT IT AS HER ACTUAL NAME.<br /><br />They’re all so bananas. There is no way anyone like any of these people exists in real life. And so what, I beg of you, is the point of examining rape culture as it exists in our world when you’re using characters who absolutely don’t?<br /><br /><br />In true Emma fashion I don’t want to talk about this anymore, so I’m going to stop now.<br /><br /><b>Bottom line</b>: As contemporaries go, this would have been a two and a half, three star read. But apparently this isn’t <i>just your average contemporary</i>, pals. It’s a fresh hell I could never have imagined.<br /><br />----------------<br />PRE-REVIEW<br /><br />so close, yet so far!!!<br /><br />shoutout to contemporaries that decide to shoot for thematic significance in the last 20 pages, leaving dozens of loose ends and not even trying for consistently feminist rhetoric!!!<br /><br />not a fan!!!!<br /><br />review to come</span>
  <a data-text-id="1159821234657538021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1608108729" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1608108729" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1608108729?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062320896" href="/book/show/28512548-the-female-of-the-species">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=important">important</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=underrated">underrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=feminist-as-fuck">feminist-as-fuck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1608108729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3141305678177596769"><i>“Physical attractiveness has nothing to do with it. You were alone, isolated, weak. It happened to you, but it could've been anyone. Opportunity is what matters, nothing else.”</i><br/><br/>I wanted to read <i>the Female of the Species</i> ever since I first saw it on Goodreads, which must've been more than a year ago. As it should happen, I was to read Mindy's newest release <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30249925.This_Darkness_Mine' title='This Darkness Mine by Mindy McGinnis' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Darkness Mine</a> before I could finally dive into TFOTS. <i>This Darkness Mine</i>; however, prepared me to have no expectations, apart from one: t</span>
  <span id="freeText3141305678177596769" style="display:none"><i>“Physical attractiveness has nothing to do with it. You were alone, isolated, weak. It happened to you, but it could've been anyone. Opportunity is what matters, nothing else.”</i><br /><br />I wanted to read <i>the Female of the Species</i> ever since I first saw it on Goodreads, which must've been more than a year ago. As it should happen, I was to read Mindy's newest release <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30249925.This_Darkness_Mine" title="This Darkness Mine by Mindy McGinnis" rel="nofollow noopener">This Darkness Mine</a> before I could finally dive into TFOTS. <i>This Darkness Mine</i>; however, prepared me to have no expectations, apart from one: they would be exceeded anyway. So much was true.<br /><br />I can only join the club of the ones praising this novel without end. For several reasons.<br />One of the being Mindy's obvious hang for writing. She has a unique and piercing style of writing, her sense of humour is subtle, often bitter and harsh, but always immensley smart. I caught myself grinning and laughing while I was reading on the underground. Other times I completely forgot the world around me and was pulled between the pages and into a story that is more captivating and distressing than anything else that I've read this year. Mindy's words can do that.<br /><br />The second reason why this book resonated so deeply with me is the strong feminist message on every written page. This story may open your eyes to internal misogyny, rape culture and slut-shaming. If they're not open to it already. Otherwise this will serve as a brutal awakening, but also as an example of what a crucial role respect and friendship play in our lives. This book will remind you that, to fight sexism and misogyny, it is important to be outspoken and direct. Staying silent helps no one, least of all yourself.<br /><br />I love that the YA book community, is so demanding it what it wants to read. That's us I'm talking about. We have only impatience for ignorance, for antiquated stories that don't represent us. We want equality and respect. We want diverse characters and depth. We demand fairness and thought. We want the real deal. And Mindy is one of the most promising authors when it comes to writing multi-layered characters and stories that matter.<br /><br />I couldn't recommend this book more. If you haven't given it any thought until now, you should put this on your list. Read it as soon as possible. Talk to me about it. I'd love to hear your thoughts.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3141305678177596769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3625306155265513158">asdfghjkl;<br/><br/>YES <br/><br/>Alex was so interesting to read about. Her inner monologue. Her tormented life. I dug it so hard. I loved that this took place in 3 different perspectives because they all added something different to the story that by the end of the book tied together so well. This book is power. Especially in a book about really lewd high schoolers that don't seem to be afraid to harass wom</span>
  <span id="freeText3625306155265513158" style="display:none">asdfghjkl;<br /><br />YES <br /><br />Alex was so interesting to read about. Her inner monologue. Her tormented life. I dug it so hard. I loved that this took place in 3 different perspectives because they all added something different to the story that by the end of the book tied together so well. This book is power. I loved it. <br /><br />If anything, I'm wary about the realisticness of the events surrounding the rapes in this book. Especially in a book about really lewd high schoolers that don't seem to be afraid to harass women, I was surprised by the author's decision to have the rapists in this book be depicted as serial rapists or drug addicts. I feel like the impact would be a lot more stark if she stuck to the fact that a lot of sexual assault happens to people you're friends with or people you know. This way, the ending wouldn't feel so..... unrealistic. Hyperbolized. Idk. I think from that angle, it could have added a lot more impact.<br /><br />Regardless, I think this book packs a punch and I read it in less than 12 hours. It's different than most YA contemporary that you'll read.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3579008382" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3579008382" />
    <a title="Dita " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26261386-dita"><img alt="Dita " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606101415p2/26261386.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3579008382?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dita " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dita " href="/user/show/26261386-dita">Dita </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3579008382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12849390589752164617">Wow, this contemporary look at rape culture was difficult to read but it was really good and I have my GR buddy, MissBecka, to thank for this gem.<br/><br/>Told from the POV of three characters: Alex, whose sister was tortured, raped and murdered, Jack a dude who is basically a penis with a guy attached and Claire, known as Peekay, a nickname short for Preacher's Kid, who is struggling to find an identity outside of her dad's job.<br/><br/>There are a few supporting characters but they are such stereotypes they don</span>
  <span id="freeText12849390589752164617" style="display:none">Wow, this contemporary look at rape culture was difficult to read but it was really good and I have my GR buddy, MissBecka, to thank for this gem.<br /><br />Told from the POV of three characters: Alex, whose sister was tortured, raped and murdered, Jack a dude who is basically a penis with a guy attached and Claire, known as Peekay, a nickname short for Preacher's Kid, who is struggling to find an identity outside of her dad's job.<br /><br />There are a few supporting characters but they are such stereotypes they don't bear much mention.<br /><br />Alex's life is defined by violence and she metes out revenge cooly and without remorse but she is also wise beyond her years, doling out advice like, "Venting yourself in an emotional moment can be more than your socially constructed self can handle after the fact."<br /><br />Is she a murderer? Yep. Did I love her? Yep.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12849390589752164617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to lily ☁️ by: </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
