        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2277614020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11598089404395029478"><blockquote>✨ <b>You can find my full review <a href='https://sprinklesofdreams.wordpress.com/2018/06/25/book-review-the-female-of-the-species-by-mindy-mcginnis/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>!</b> ✨</blockquote><br/>You know those books—the ones you finish, and afterwards you come out of the experience feeling like you are a different person, and you can’t quite remember who exactly you were before? “Some books you read. Some books you enjoy. But <b>some books just swallow you up, heart and soul</b>,” Joanne Harris once said.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25812109.The_Female_of_the_Species' title='The Female of the Species by Mindy McGinnis' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Female of the Species</a> is that book. <br/><br/>The kind of book that leaves you lying in bed at night, staring at the ceiling blankly, while contemplating your ex</span>
  <span id="freeText11598089404395029478" style="display:none"><blockquote>✨ <b>You can find my full review <a href="https://sprinklesofdreams.wordpress.com/2018/06/25/book-review-the-female-of-the-species-by-mindy-mcginnis/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>!</b> ✨</blockquote><br />You know those books—the ones you finish, and afterwards you come out of the experience feeling like you are a different person, and you can’t quite remember who exactly you were before? “Some books you read. Some books you enjoy. But <b>some books just swallow you up, heart and soul</b>,” Joanne Harris once said.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25812109.The_Female_of_the_Species" title="The Female of the Species by Mindy McGinnis" rel="nofollow noopener">The Female of the Species</a> is that book. <br /><br />The kind of book that leaves you lying in bed at night, staring at the ceiling blankly, while contemplating your existence and everything else you ever thought you knew.<br /><br />“Oh, another book that talks about rape”, some people will inevitably think, and scoff, rolling their eyes, their thoughts probably ending somewhere along the lines of “haven’t we had enough of those already?” <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The answer is no. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />But even so, <i>The Female of the Species</i> would not simply be “just another book that talks about rape”; it does examine rape culture, yes, but it also explores friendships, and loyalty, it talks about morals, courage, love, and it shines a light on feminism, and so many other issues that contemporaries should shine a light on, but unfortunately rarely do. And it does so flawlessly, and boldly.<br /><br /><blockquote><i>“But </i>boys will be boys<i>, our favorite phrase that excuses so many things, while the only thing we have for the opposite gender is </i>women<i>, said with disdain and punctuated with an eye roll.”</i></blockquote><br />Do not let yourself be fooled by the tame, almost cute cover—cute is the least likely adjective I would use to describe the contents; this book is dark, and gritty, and full of angst. But it is also honest, hopeful, and filled with love, and compassion.<br /><br />I have read my fair share of books dealing with rape, a few of which I already deemed immensely well-written, but this one … I feel like it carved out a hole in my chest, and left behind an emptiness that I don’t know how to fill, and <b>I don’t know if I will ever stop hurting from it.</b><br /><br /><a href="https://sprinklesofdreams.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="http://twitter.com/sprnklsofdreams" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/sprinklesofdreamsx/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://sprinklesofdreams.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/sprinkles-dreams-19449885" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11598089404395029478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1380339579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8268928486397689833"><blockquote>
  <i>Everyone thinks if you fix a male dog it will lower his aggression, but most of the biters are female. It’s basic instinct to protect their womb. You see it in all animals - the female of the species is more deadly than the male.</i>
</blockquote><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25812109.The_Female_of_the_Species' title='The Female of the Species by Mindy McGinnis' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Female of the Species</a> is a bit harder to review because of how important a book it is. It’s a story exploring rape culture, the effects of sexual assault, over-sexualization of teenagers, gender issues, sexual objectification, and slut-shaming. Set in Ohio with </span>
  <span id="freeText8268928486397689833" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Everyone thinks if you fix a male dog it will lower his aggression, but most of the biters are female. It’s basic instinct to protect their womb. You see it in all animals - the female of the species is more deadly than the male.</i>
</blockquote><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25812109.The_Female_of_the_Species" title="The Female of the Species by Mindy McGinnis" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Female of the Species</a> is a bit harder to review because of how important a book it is. It’s a story exploring rape culture, the effects of sexual assault, over-sexualization of teenagers, gender issues, sexual objectification, and slut-shaming. Set in Ohio with alternating perspectives from Alex, Jack and Peekay.<br /><br />Alex Craft’s sister Anna was raped and murdered three years ago. Due to lack of evidence, the killer walks free. Alex refuses to let that happen and gets away with her crime. Her impulses cause her to live under the radar. Known only as “the girl with the dead sister” to her classmates until forming her first friendship and things unfold from there. She’s the vigilante of the book - the one out for justice! I loved her dark nature, but also her instinct to protect those in need and come to their defense. She’s a character to be admired.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Let her know that Anna was on the minds of everyone today. Something that rightfully belongs to only us resurrected once again as a cautionary fairy tale, a warning to all of the Little Red Riding Hoods that there are wolves in the forest.</i>
</blockquote><br />Jack is the star athlete on track for valedictorian. He’s that guy who loves girls. He also happened to be there in a crass sort of way the night Anna’s body was discovered, so he feels bad for his part. He wants so badly to get to know Alex.<br /><br />Peekay is the preacher’s kid who was recently dumped for Branley leading to plenty of slut-shaming moments. She is doing her Senior Year Experience at the animal shelter with Alex who may be the first person to see her in a different light that doesn’t scream “daughter of preacher.” A beautiful friendship is developed.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Because there are others like him still. Tonight they used words they know, words that don't bother people anymore. They said bitch. They told another girl they would put their dicks in her mouth. No one protested because this is our language now.</i>
</blockquote><br />Humanity is examined. Human nature vs animal nature. Instinct. Violence. The world we allow ourselves to live in because some of these actions are viewed as “normal.” Or when we let him get away with it because wearing that short skirt is “asking for it.”<br /><br />It’s quite eye-opening to those who have never experienced what it is like to be a woman. I explained a few different instances where I was sexually harassed in “minor” ways to my significant other and he was shocked that being a female opens you up to that kind of treatment. But it’s real and it happens. Being a teenager, you think you’re as mature and knowing as it gets, but you’re not. And being told you have to go further and have sex with someone or they won’t take you home is NOT okay. Date rape is not okay. Any form of making you feel like your body is not yours and yours alone is wrong. This book brought out emotions in me I didn’t know I still had. It took me to a deeper place I’m usually too afraid to go. I found myself envious of Alex, not because she was a vigilante but because she did something about it.<br /><br />I cannot recommend this book enough for the relevance of it’s message. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5351825.Mindy_McGinnis" title="Mindy McGinnis" rel="nofollow noopener"> Mindy McGinnis</a> presents it in a way that is beautifully written, dark, and impactful. Highly recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8268928486397689833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1853119325" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1853119325" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1853119325?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1853119325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9273710534724554040">I have <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/6857324-lauren-stoolfire' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lauren</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/32799998-erin-patton' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Erin</a> to thank for this one!<br/><br/>"This is how I kill someone. I learn his habits, I know his schedule. It is not difficult. His life consists of quick stops to the dollar store for the bare minimum of things required to keep this ragged cycle going, his hat pulled down over his eyes so as not to be recognized. But he is. It's a small town."<br/><br/>Alex Craft's life was turned upside down three years earlier when her older sister Anna was murdered. The killer was exonerated, but it was clear </span>
  <span id="freeText9273710534724554040" style="display:none">I have <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/6857324-lauren-stoolfire" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Lauren</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/32799998-erin-patton" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Erin</a> to thank for this one!<br /><br />"This is how I kill someone. I learn his habits, I know his schedule. It is not difficult. His life consists of quick stops to the dollar store for the bare minimum of things required to keep this ragged cycle going, his hat pulled down over his eyes so as not to be recognized. But he is. It's a small town."<br /><br />Alex Craft's life was turned upside down three years earlier when her older sister Anna was murdered. The killer was exonerated, but it was clear to nearly everyone in their small town that he was guilty. Alex takes matters into her own hands, and the killer was found brutally tortured and murdered. But no one seems particularly broken up about it, and if anyone suspects Alex, their suspicions go nowhere.<br /><br />As she goes through high school, she keeps to herself. She's known as the girl with the murdered sister, and she keeps herself occupied by reading and running. She doesn't mind her lonely existence—the fact is, she doesn't really trust herself around other people, because if she finds someone who raises her anger for a serious crime, she might act again in the way she did with her sister's killer. She doesn't have a problem with that, honestly, but she knows others will.<br /><br />"I'm not fine, and I doubt I ever will be. The books didn't help me find a word for myself; my father refused to accept the weight of it. And so I made my own. I am vengeance."<br /><br />While Alex steels herself for another situation that might provoke her instincts, she is utterly unprepared for connecting with other people, and senior year brings two intense connections—Peekay, the slightly rebellious preacher's daughter, who befriends Alex when they volunteer at an animal shelter, and Jack, the school's top athlete and biggest playboy, who is drawn to Alex in ways even he can't understand, and to the distinct satisfaction of his longtime friend-with-benefits, star cheerleader (and most beautiful girl in school), Branley.<br /><br />Peekay awakens Alex's protective nature (and causes her to step outside her comfort zone), and Jack actually makes her feel special, feel wanted, feel as if what makes her so different than everyone else might not be such a deal-breaker after all.<br /><br />But as senior year unfolds, and Alex's relationships intensify with both Peekay and Jack, she realizes she cannot hide who she really is, what she is driven to do. She tries as hard as she can, but her need to avenge mistreatment, violence, wrongdoing by taking matters into her own hands always wins out. She doesn't want there to be secrets, especially between her and Jack, but she knows if he discovers who she really is, they have no chance at a future anyway, so she may as well fulfill the role she feels destined to.<br /><br />"There are parts of yourself that you hate; parts that you know other people wouldn't understand."<br /><br />All I can say about this book is holy crap. (And that's a cleaned-up version.) This seems to be a year of unforgettable, unique characters—Letty Dobesh in Blake Crouch's <b>
  <i>Good Behavior</i>
</b>; Julian in Robin Roe's <b>
  <i>A List of Cages</i>
</b>; Ivan Isaenko in Scott Stambach's <b>
  <i>The Invisible Life of Ivan Isaenko</i>
</b>; and Evan Smoak in Gregg Hurwitz's <b>
  <i>Orphan X</i>
</b>, just to name a few. Yet no character is like Alex Craft. She's like a cross between Lisbeth Salander and Dexter, but with more vulnerability and heart. (And I say that not to discount this book as simply a gruesome thriller, because it is so much more than that.)<br /><br />Mindy McGinnis does something I've not seen in a book recently, particularly a YA book: she conveys a strong message without making the story heavy-handed or preachy. While she clearly isn't recommending that people avenge murder, rape, and other violence, she is saying that women (and men) shouldn't allow themselves to live in fear or shame, to remain a victim. I hope that message reaches the ears of those who need to hear it.<br /><br />I thought this book was really amazing. It's certainly not for everyone, and it's not realistic, but that didn't detract from its appeal in any way. This is book with tremendous heart and emotion, suspense, and some violence which might be troubling for some. But McGinnis knows how to tell a story that hooked me from start to finish, and it's a story populated by characters I won't soon forget. Truly a home run, as far as I'm concerned.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com">http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blo...</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9273710534724554040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2761901082" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2761901082" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2761901082?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062320902" href="/book/show/33385391-the-female-of-the-species">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik?shelf=best-ones">best-ones</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2761901082" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16974472857818199869">5 is not enough, it deserves 10 brutal, brilliant, heart wrenching stars!<br/><br/>This book is not an easy read! It tears your heart apart! It punches you several times on the face! It makes you cry aloud ! Your emotions scatter all over the places when you’re reading it!<br/><br/>Raw, realistic, violent, dark but definitely fantastic!<br/>Alex is so far a different girl who only wants to be normal, she doesn’t deserve be acknowledged by her dead sister’s name, she deserves friendship, she deserves love, she deserves j</span>
  <span id="freeText16974472857818199869" style="display:none">5 is not enough, it deserves 10 brutal, brilliant, heart wrenching stars!<br /><br />This book is not an easy read! It tears your heart apart! It punches you several times on the face! It makes you cry aloud ! Your emotions scatter all over the places when you’re reading it!<br /><br />Raw, realistic, violent, dark but definitely fantastic!<br />Alex is so far a different girl who only wants to be normal, she doesn’t deserve be acknowledged by her dead sister’s name, she deserves friendship, she deserves love, she deserves joy, happiness in her life. She deserves to go to college because she’s real smart. But she cannot! Because she cannot fight with her killer instincts and she cannot function as like a young girl who dreams her HEA. <br /><br />Her character is definitely not Dexter. She is not sociopath, cause she feels too much and she cannot know how to deal with her feelings. She knows how to defeat the real demons in outside world but she has no idea how to defeat her inner demons . That’s what seals her destiny. <br /><br />I’ve been totally shaken after the shocking end. But I have to admit that is fair ending of the story. <br /><br />Some books take your piece of soul and leave unforgettable emotional scar on your hearts. It is definitely that kind of book! I loved it so much but the words and story hurt me so much, too.<br /><br /><a href="https://niluferozmekik.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/nilylovestoread/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a><br /><a href="https://www.facebook.com/nilufer.ozmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/NiluferOzmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a></span>

<div id="review_1992042397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1992042397" />
    <a title="Wren (fablesandwren)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42780417-wren-fablesandwren"><img alt="Wren (fablesandwren)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596719528p2/42780417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1992042397?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wren (fablesandwren)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wren (fablesandwren)" href="/user/show/42780417-wren-fablesandwren">Wren (fablesandwren)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062320896" href="/book/show/28512548-the-female-of-the-species">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=not-shelved">not-shelved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=04-stars">04-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1992042397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8074600462091706933"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519097769i/25090443.jpg' alt='' width='300' height='300' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>*featuring the female of my duo, Marcy Louisa and all her fluff*</i><br/><br/>This was the February Read for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/270328-the-cheerful-wednesdays?ref=nav_bar_discussions_pane_group' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Cheerful Wednesdays</a>, and might I say that this was a heavy book. <br/><br/>This book is full of all kinds of <b>triggers</b>. There is talk of murder, rape, child pornography, animal cruelty, substance abuse and just about anything you can think of. Some of these are actual topics that should be talked about more in order for people to understand them, and for this I thank the author for not shying away from the to</span>
  <span id="freeText8074600462091706933" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519097769i/25090443.jpg" alt="" width="300" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>*featuring the female of my duo, Marcy Louisa and all her fluff*</i><br><br>This was the February Read for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/270328-the-cheerful-wednesdays?ref=nav_bar_discussions_pane_group" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cheerful Wednesdays</a>, and might I say that this was a heavy book. <br><br>This book is full of all kinds of <b>triggers</b>. There is talk of murder, rape, child pornography, animal cruelty, substance abuse and just about anything you can think of. Some of these are actual topics that should be talked about more in order for people to understand them, and for this I thank the author for not shying away from the tougher topics.<br><br>“You see it in all animals - the female of the species is more deadly than the male. <b>Except humans</b>.” <br><br>Alex is dealing with a lot. Her sister was brutally killed and raped and left in the woods for someone to find days later after nature took her course on her. Ever since then, she has not been the same. She doesn't actually know if she changed because of what happened or she is the way she is because her sister was the only thing holding her to the ground; but what she does know is a simple rule: <b>people who hurt other people deserve to die,</b> and ladies and gentlemen, she is true to her word.<br><br>See, Alex is 100% a murderer but in a Dexter-type of way. She only takes out the <u>absolute</u> <b>trash</b> of the world. She has a heart and she feels things too, but she lives off of her animal instinct. You kill those who hurt others in order to protect people. Unlike Dexter, she doesn't actually have to kill, she just is driven when the opportunity arises. <br><br>So what happens when Alex volunteers at an animal shelter and meets the pastor's kid, Peekay? She learns what it is like to have a friend.<br><br>Peekay is tired of always being associated with being the pastor's kid. She doesn't have a problem with the religion and she loves her parents with all her heart, but she wants to be known for something else for a change. With a recent break up, Peekay finds hope in her new friend and the challenges that come up along the way. <br><br>Alex and Peekay are friendship goals. They support each other, they pick each other up, and there is no "frienemies" involved. They just love and support each other, which is something a lot of our culture has lacked. Women pin each other against each other and are jealous of what they can't have. I think Alex was a refreshing break for Peekay because Alex never expected anything and was always just there to help her. They both found themselves again in their friendship which is what friendship is actually about. <br><br>“<i>But boys will be boys, our favorite phrase that excuses so many things, while the only thing we have for the opposite gender is women, said with disdain and punctuated with an eye roll.</i>”<br><br>Now I am not going to lie, I got really, <i>really</i> weird vibes from Jack. I'm not sure if it was just because the author actually got into the mind of a man and went with it, or because he is actually creepy... but I will let you figure that one out yourself. His character does have some growth in it, but honestly I just didn't find him appealing. He was kind of... gross to me. Which leads me to believe that crawling into the mind of a man will literally kill all romantic notions. <br><br>One thing that really made me uncomfortable was the brutality with the animals in this book. Jack works with the butcher and is the one that takes the life of the cows, Alex and Peekay pick up dead baby animals that were thrown out of a moving vehicle... I could have lived without all those visuals and I am sorry I just put those in your head when you were 100% not asking for it. Even the emotional sadness with animals in this book almost made me just put the book down. <br><br><u>Little background on me</u>: I've been a vegetarian since I was 08 years old. Some days, I am vegan. You can bet your bottom dollar I eat like my namesake: a bird. I have two rescued cats and I love all animals to the absolute fullest. I even take the time to get on Amazon Smile to make sure it donates to my appointed rescue. You can say I am a little bit of a nut job, but I am a full believer of taking care of the creatures I was put on this earth to take care of (and that also includes the earth itself... also a big recycler). <br><br>Now don't get me wrong, I will touch and make meat and I am not going to even give your food a second glance if you are eating a cheeseburger in front of me. But <b>I never want to read about someone actually in the process of making the food that the majority of the world eats ever again</b>. It was too heartbreaking for this tender-heart bird.<br><br>Which brings up another dilemma of mine: why did the talk of animals being killed hurt more than the idea of some of the other topics in this book? Am I that filtered? When I have talked to some of the other people who have read this book, they all felt the same way I did. Why is it that the talk of someone killing an animal is more repulsive than the talk of someone killing another human? I can watch Criminal Minds all day, but I will never watch Old Yeller again. I love war movies, but you will see me plug my ears and close my eyes when it is apparent that a horse is about to die. <br><br>I'm just bringing all of that up because I don't want people to think that I am pointing fingers. This is also a topic that I need to learn more about and talk openly with. This book is a good start to ease someone into this kind of topic and also a great one to read with a few people. I read this with my book club <a href="http://wrensreads.com/index.php/the-cheerful-wednesdays/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cheerful Wednesdays</a>, and I can tell you that none of us expected this book to go as deep as it did. <br><br>Overall, this book was just a really, really heavy read. I didn't resonate with the ending too well, and I am not sure if it was because I didn't like it or because I knew it was the only way for this story to conclude. Even if you took out the romance in this book, the friendship between Alex and Peekay is worth the read. Even if you took out both the romance and the friendship, the topics touched on are worth reading and learning about. <br><br>- - - <br><br>This book is so...incredibly...heavy <br><br>2/3rds in and man, do I have so many emotions. <br><br>I feel as if I need to go smell the flowers and appreciate those people in my life who bring good things to it and possibly punch everyone who doesn’t.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8074600462091706933" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1656698109">

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1698834875" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32799998-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469767858p2/32799998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1698834875?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/32799998-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32799998-erin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32799998-erin?shelf=best-ya">best-ya</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1698834875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7237704110819223416">WOW!!! Don't let the title fool you. The Female of the Species is dark, brutal, & deadly. Mindy McGinnis weaves a tale of teenage angst, vigilante justice, & the pervasiveness of rape culture. I read this book with a knot the size of a fist in my stomach. I have a feeling I'll be thinking about the book for a long time. I recommend this book to all my fellow females & anyone who knows a female.</span>
  <span id="freeText7237704110819223416" style="display:none">WOW!!! Don't let the title fool you. The Female of the Species is dark, brutal, &amp; deadly. Mindy McGinnis weaves a tale of teenage angst, vigilante justice, &amp; the pervasiveness of rape culture. I read this book with a knot the size of a fist in my stomach. I have a feeling I'll be thinking about the book for a long time. I recommend this book to all my fellow females &amp; anyone who knows a female.</span>

<div id="review_1320875370" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1320875370" />
    <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters"><img alt="Trina (Between Chapters)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530495507p2/9323164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1320875370?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trina (Between Chapters)" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters">Trina (Between Chapters)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062320896" href="/book/show/28512548-the-female-of-the-species">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=standalones">standalones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=2016-favorites">2016-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1320875370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9110790690399685179">This book is an examination of rape culture. What if you knew your sister or your friend had been sexually assaulted? What if there's not enough evidence for the police to do anything? Would you think about taking matters into your own hands to get revenge? That's what this book is. It's the wish fulfillment of avenging sex crimes.<br/><br/>There are 3 points of view in this book:<br/><br/>There's Alex, the girl who takes revenge. Who sees someone get roofied and throws the first punch. She's the anti-hero, the mor</span>
  <span id="freeText9110790690399685179" style="display:none">This book is an examination of rape culture. What if you knew your sister or your friend had been sexually assaulted? What if there's not enough evidence for the police to do anything? Would you think about taking matters into your own hands to get revenge? That's what this book is. It's the wish fulfillment of avenging sex crimes.<br /><br />There are 3 points of view in this book:<br /><br />There's Alex, the girl who takes revenge. Who sees someone get roofied and throws the first punch. She's the anti-hero, the morally gray character extracting vigilante justice.<br /><br />There's Jack, our example of the male gaze. The inside look at 'boys will be boys.' The one who starts to feel bad for that kind of behavior.<br /><br />And then there's Peekay (P.K.), the rebellious preacher's daughter who doesn't think much about how she puts other girls down. Who doesn't think much about taking drinks from strangers.<br /><br />While it might seem at first that this book is kind of crass, or slut-shaming, I quickly came to realize that we had to see those examples in order for the book to start making points about them. The way that each of these characters learn from each other was a really beautiful thing.<br /><br />There are many examinations of what separates human-nature from animal-nature, the difference in violent thought versus violent behavior, and what makes something right or wrong? If you've read anything else by Mindy McGinnis, you are getting that same soul-wrenching examination of humanity.<br /><br />It's no secret that Mindy is one of my favorite authors, and this book just further cemented that. She took on a few new things this time: Contemporary genre, multiple POVs, male POV, more romance than usual. And she SLAYED them. <br /><br />I not only loved the writing and the characters, but how there was so much to unpack from this book. It gave me a lot to digest and think about beyond just the words on the page. I really enjoyed it and thought it was well crafted.<br /><br />Some things worth noting, content wise: there are descriptions of sexual assault, animal injuries, and gore. Heads up if those are personal triggers, but none of them are used superfluously.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9110790690399685179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2586653150" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2586653150" />
    <a title="Felicia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13169794-felicia"><img alt="Felicia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464034900p2/13169794.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2586653150?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Felicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Felicia" href="/user/show/13169794-felicia">Felicia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2586653150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8998256656515944249">“But boys will be boys, our favorite phrase that excuses so many things, while the only thing we have for the opposite gender is women, said with disdain and punctuated with an eye roll.”<br/><br/>Read that quote again. And after reading it again you don't get tears in your eyes, not from pain but from anger, then you need to read it again.<br/><br/>I went into this book completely blind after having it recommended to me by a Goodreads friend. I didn't know what it was about, I didn't read any reviews and I think t</span>
  <span id="freeText8998256656515944249" style="display:none">“But boys will be boys, our favorite phrase that excuses so many things, while the only thing we have for the opposite gender is women, said with disdain and punctuated with an eye roll.”<br /><br />Read that quote again. And after reading it again you don't get tears in your eyes, not from pain but from anger, then you need to read it again.<br /><br />I went into this book completely blind after having it recommended to me by a Goodreads friend. I didn't know what it was about, I didn't read any reviews and I think that decision added to the power of this book.<br /><br />This story sneaks up on you. What I initially thought was going to be another typical YA thriller became anything but. <br /><br />The author doesn't present the complexities of this story in an overt manner. She stealthily plants ideas into your psyche that slowly start to change your perception until, without notice or permission, you're presented with a horrifying reality that makes you question everything you've ever been taught and have taught to the girls and young women in your life.<br /><br />This book is required reading for teen girls and the people responsible for their well-being. Parents, teachers, family and friends. <br /><br />This story is the #metoo movement told in a way that is relatable to girls. It's empowering and eye-opening and teaches girls that what they've been conditioned to see as normal and as boys being boys is NOT OKAY. <br /><br />I think the most profound lesson in this story is that girls have a voice and it's important to use it, to stand up when you see or experience something that makes you uncomfortable. Using your voice just once can ultimately save someone's life, can change a turn of events and, in time, can change the world <br /><br />"You see it in all animals—the female of the species is more deadly than the male.”<br /><br />Damn straight.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8998256656515944249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Za7wJA0BImywq+5aPp7CAI6NnSj+2Pdj28d+RZgWG7JlWij/0D9x4a+WtwqCzKkrrK7bmWv8NTgWWEauHqFHow==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('B6z7bO5n2h5gKyI0dqFDXF59ANhLlpKtNbyUmqhOA9UHWCO3M1mJk38We2TK8yh3fF5Gad6yUPb4I6xxLvlfxA==')})
  }
